The Human Body as Proof of a Wise Creator
Ibn Zakariyya argues human body design proves a wise Creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the intricate design of the human body, as argued by Muhammad ibn Zakariyya, rationally necessitates a Wise Creator, and why attributing such design to blind nature is unreasonable.

Core Idea
The human body's design is so wondrous that reason demands a wise Creator.

Muhammad ibn Zakariyya, after presenting a previous analogy (the water jug), turns to the human body itself. He describes its intricate compositions and forms, each corresponding to wisdom and benefit. Then he declares that plain reason testifies that such marvels cannot originate except from a powerful and wise Creator. This passage shows how teleological arguments from design are grounded in rational necessity, not mere speculation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's rhythm and argument come through.
Notice the progression from description to conclusion to dismissal of alternatives.
2
Identify the key elements
Identify the wondrous compositions, forms corresponding to wisdom, and the testimony of plain reason. See how these lead to the conclusion of a wise Creator.
3
Contrast with the alternative
Note how the author likens the naturalistic explanation to hiding the sun with dust. Understand the futility attributed to such attempts.
This contrast strengthens the rational necessity of the design argument.
4
Reflect on rational necessity
Reflect on why, for Ibn Zakariyya, the design is so evident that reason cannot accept a naturalistic explanation. This is the core of the teleological argument.
The argument is not merely probable but rationally compelling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن محمد بن زكريا بعد أن ذكر هذا المقال الحسن، الموافق للمقصود، شرع في شرح آثار حكمة الرحمن في تخليق بدن الإنسان، وذكر بعض ما فيه من التركيبات العجيبة والهيئات المطابقة للحكمة والمصلحة، ثم قال بعدها: وصريح العقل شاهد بأن هذه العجائب والبدائع في تركيب هذا البدن لا يمكن صدورها إلا عن قادر حكيم خلق هذه البنية بقدرته، وأحكمها بحكمته. واعلم أن هذا البيان الذي ذكره محمد بن زكريا في هذا الموضع بيان حسن كامل، وعند هذا يظهر للعقل السليم: أن هذه الوجوه المتكلفة المذكورة في بيان أنه يجوز صدور هذه الآثار العجيبة الحاصلة في تخليق بدن الإنسان عن الطبيعة المحضة، الخالية عن العلم والقدرة: وجوه ضعيفة خسيسة جارية مجرى إخفاء قرص الشمس بكف من التراب.
Then Muhammad ibn Zakariyya, after mentioning this good article consistent with the purpose, proceeded to explain the traces of the wisdom of the Merciful in the creation of the human body, and mentioned some of the wondrous compositions and forms corresponding to wisdom and benefit. Then he said after that: 'Plain reason testifies that these marvels and wonders in the composition of this body cannot originate except from a powerful and wise [creator] who created this structure with His power and perfected it with His wisdom.' And know that this explanation that Muhammad ibn Zakariyya mentioned in this place is a good and perfect explanation, and by this it becomes evident to the sound intellect that these forced aspects mentioned in explaining that it is possible for these wondrous effects occurring in the creation of the human body to originate from sheer nature, devoid of knowledge and power, are weak and base aspects, running in the course of concealing the disk of the sun with a handful of dust.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage reports that Muhammad ibn Zakariyya, after presenting the water jug analogy, turns to the human body. He describes its wondrous compositions and forms, all perfectly suited for wisdom and benefit. He then states that plain reason testifies that such marvels cannot come from anything but a powerful and wise Creator. The author affirms that this explanation is excellent and perfect. The passage then contrasts this with the weak alternative explanations that attribute these effects to sheer nature without knowledge or power, likening such attempts to hiding the sun with a handful of dust—an absurd and futile effort.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that design arguments are merely weak analogies or probabilistic inferences that can be easily dismissed.
Correction: This passage presents the design argument as a rational necessity: plain reason testifies that such intricate design cannot come from blind nature. The author dismisses naturalistic explanations as utterly futile, like hiding the sun.

Checkpoint

A) That it could have formed by chance over time.

D) That the human body is not as complex as a jug.

Key Takeaway
The intricate design of the human body compels reason to acknowledge a wise Creator, and any attempt to attribute it to blind nature is as futile as trying to hide the sun with dust.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage says attributing the marvels of your body to blind nature is like trying to hide the sun with dust. Do you ever live as if your existence is random or accidental, forgetting the wise purpose behind every detail? What would change if you fully believed that every breath is a sign of a powerful and wise Creator?
?
If plain reason itself testifies that such a body cannot exist without a wise Creator, then why do you sometimes hesitate to acknowledge His presence in the ordinary moments of your life? What is the 'dust' you use to cover the sun of His signs?

Quranic Refutation of Attributing Creation to Nature
Quranic refutation of attributing creation to blind nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a Quranic argument refutes the idea that nature alone is responsible for creation, and why attributing creation to blind nature is a denial of self-evident truths.

Core Idea
Blind nature cannot create; divine wisdom governs creation.

This lesson examines a key Quranic passage (al-Mursalat 77:20-24) that refutes those who attribute creation to impersonal nature. The verse describes the detailed process of human embryonic development, showing that it requires deliberate management and cannot be the result of blind natural forces. The commentary explains the logical implications and the consequence of denying this.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verse
Read the verse in Arabic and translation. Notice how it describes the creation of humans from a despised fluid and the stages of development.
2
Understand 'until a known measure'
The commentary explains that the seminal fluid would normally be lost, but divine management retains it in the womb for a specific period. See how this refutes naturalistic causation.
The retention and expulsion are both divinely managed.
3
Reflect on the consequence for deniers
The verse ends with a warning to those who deny. The commentary explains that attributing these wise actions to a nature without sensation or power is a denial of self-evident truths. Consider why this is a powerful argument.
This shows that naturalism contradicts basic rationality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال تعالى في الكتاب الإلهي: ألم نخلقكم من ماء مهين؟ فجعلناه في قرار مكين، إلى قدر معلوم، فقدرنا فنعم القادرون، ويل يومئذ للمكذبين. فقوله: (فجعلناه في قرار مكين، إلى قدر معلوم) معناه: أن طبيعة المني تقتضي النقل والزوال، إلا إذا دبر خلقه في الرحم تدبيراً عجيباً يقتضي استمساك تلك القطرة في الحريم، إنا دبرنا خلقة ذلك العضو بحيث يقتضي استمساكها إلى حد معين، وزمان معلوم، وهو المدة التي يحتاج الجنين فيها إلى الاستكمال والتمام، فإذا تم البدن وكملت الخلقة زال ذلك الاستمساك، وبطل ذلك الحفظ، وانقلبت الطبيعة الحافظة الممسكة إلى مرسلة مخرجة، وعند ذلك ينفصل الولد عن الرحم. فقوله: (إلى قدر معلوم) إشارة إلى أن بقاء ذلك الجسم في الموضع المعلوم، ممتداً إلى مقدار الحاجة، فإذا انقضى زمان الحاجة، لم يبق الاستقرار في ذلك الموضع. ثم قال: (ويل يومئذ للمكذبين) يعني من عرف أن هذه أفعال واقعة على وجه الحكمة، والرحمة، وإفاضة النعمة. ثم إن إنساناً لو أضافها إلى طبيعة لا شعور لها ولا إدراك، ولا قدرة على فعل من الأفعال، كان ذلك مكذباً بالعلوم البديهية، وجاحداً للمعارف اليقينية، فيكون مستحقاً للويل والبلاء.
He, exalted, said in the divine Book: 'Did We not create you from a despised fluid? Then We placed it in a secure resting place, until a known measure, and We determined [it] and excellent are the determiners. Woe that Day to the deniers.' So His saying: 'Then We placed it in a secure resting place, until a known measure' means that the nature of the seminal fluid requires movement and disappearance, unless its creation is managed in the womb with a wondrous management that necessitates the retention of that drop in the womb—indeed We managed the creation of that organ such that it necessitates its retention until a specific limit and known time, which is the period during which the fetus needs completion and perfection. When the body is completed and the creation perfected, that retention ceases, that preservation is nullified, and the preservative, retentive nature turns into a releasing, expelling one, and at that point the child separates from the womb. So His saying: 'until a known measure' indicates that the staying of that body in the known place extends to the amount of need, and when the time of need passes, there is no longer stability in that place. Then He said: 'Woe that Day to the deniers,' meaning whoever knows that these are actions occurring in accordance with wisdom, mercy, and effusion of grace. Then if a person were to attribute them to a nature without sensation, perception, or power to do any action, that would be a denial of axiomatic sciences and a rejection of certain knowledge, and thus he deserves woe and tribulation.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage presents a Quranic argument against attributing creation to blind nature. The verse (al-Mursalat 77:20-24) is cited: 'Did We not create you from a despised fluid...' The author interprets 'until a known measure' as meaning that the seminal fluid, by its nature, would dissipate, but divine management retains it in the womb for a specific period until the fetus is complete, after which it is expelled. The verse ends with 'Woe that Day to the deniers' — referring to those who, despite knowing these actions are wise and merciful, attribute them to a nature devoid of sensation and power. Such attribution is a denial of self-evident truths and certain knowledge, deserving of punishment.

Key Terms
طبيعة المني
تدبير عجيب
استمساك
العلوم البديهية
المعارف اليقينية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Creation occurs solely through the blind, impersonal forces of nature without any divine intervention.
Correction: The Quranic verse and commentary demonstrate that the precise management of embryonic development requires intentional design and cannot be the result of unconscious nature.

Checkpoint

A) It remains in the womb indefinitely.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic argument shows that the intricate process of human creation cannot be attributed to blind nature, and doing so is a denial of self-evident truths.

Refuting the Intellect/Soul as Agent – The Necessity of the Necessary Being
Al-Razi refutes the intellect/soul objection and concludes with the Necessary Existent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Fakhr al-Din al-Razi refutes the objection that intellect or soul could be the agent of celestial spheres and planets, and why the argument leads necessarily to the Necessary Existent in itself.

Core Idea
Any contingent agent demands a Necessary End – circularity and infinite regress are impossible.

In this passage, al-Razi responds to a specific objection: why not attribute the specific characteristics of celestial spheres and planets to an intellect or soul rather than directly to God? He shows that this only postpones the question, because any contingent being requires a cause, and the causal chain must terminate in a Necessary Being. This argument is a classic application of the impossibility of infinite regress (tasalsul) and circularity (dawr) in causation, and it anchors the entire discussion in the Quranic verse 'And that to your Lord is the final end.'

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's argument flow naturally before interpreting.
The text contains a small textual uncertainty (marked with [?]), but it does not affect the overall argument.
2
Identify the objection and the author's response
Notice how al-Razi first restates the conclusion that bodies are similar in essence, so their specific characteristics must come from God. Then he presents the objection: 'Why not an intellect or soul?' and acknowledges its possibility before countering it.
The response is not a rejection of the possibility but a logical follow-up showing it leads to the same conclusion.
3
Follow the logical chain: contingent → cause → necessary
The key move: if the intellect/soul is possible in existence (mumkin al-wujud), it depends on a cause. Since circularity and infinite regress are invalid, the chain must end with the Necessary Existent. If it is itself necessary, then it is God.
This is the central argument that refutes the objection without disproving the possibility.
4
Reflect on the Quranic conclusion
The author quotes Surah al-Najm 42: 'And that to your Lord is the final end.' Reflect on why he calls this word the fountain of goods and the center of benefits. Consider how this verse encapsulates the entire argument.
The conclusion is both philosophical and scriptural, grounding rational theology in revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لكنا لما بينا أن الأجسام متماثلة ، فحينئذ يظهر لنا : أن اختصاص كل فلك ، وكل كوكب بصفته المعينة وخاصيته المعينة إنما كان بتخليق الإله الحكيم ، وعلى هذا التقدير فلا يضرنا هذا الكلام. وأما قوله : « لم لا يجوز أن يكون فاعل هذه التركيبات عقل ونفس : ؟ قلنا : هذا الاحتمال قائم . إلا أنا نقول : ذلك العقل أو النفس ، إن كان ممكن الوجود افتقر إلى السبب، والدور والتسلسل باطلان ، فلا بد من الانتهاء إلى واجب الوجود لذاته وإن كان ذلك الشيء واجب الوجود فهو المقصود . واعلم أن الحرف [؟] المعدات للحاجات والضرورات ، لا تندفع إلا بالانتهاء ، إلى واجب الوجود لذاته ، فلهذا السبب جاء في الكتاب الإلهي قوله تعالى : ( وأن إلى ربك المنتهى ) ومن تأمل على الوجه الحقيقي عرف أن هذه الكلمة ينبوع الخيرات ومركز المصالح والسعادات وبالله التوفيق
But when we explained that bodies are similar, then it becomes clear to us: that the specification of each sphere and each planet with its determined quality and its determined property was only by the creation of the wise God. On this estimation, this speech does not harm us. As for his statement: 'Why is it not permissible that the agent of these compositions be an intellect and a soul?' We said: This possibility stands. However, we say: That intellect or soul, if it is possible in existence, it is in need of a cause, and circularity and infinite regress are invalid. So it is necessary to end at the Necessary Existent in itself. And if that thing is Necessary Existent, then it is the intended. And know that the [؟] which prepare needs and necessities are not repelled except by ending at the Necessary Existent in itself. For this reason it came in the divine book, His statement the Exalted: 'And that to your Lord is the final end.' And whoever reflects in the true manner knows that this word is the fountain of goods and the center of benefits and happinesses. And with Allah is the success.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection and a conclusion. The author first restates the premise that bodies are similar in essence, so the specific characteristics of each celestial sphere and planet must come from the wise Creator. Then he addresses an objection: "Why not allow that the agent of these compositions is an intellect or a soul?" The author acknowledges the possibility but counters that such an intellect or soul, if it is contingent in existence (i.e., not necessary), would require a cause. Since circular causation and infinite regress are invalid, the chain must end with the Necessary Existent in itself (واجب الوجود لذاته). If that intellect or soul is itself necessary, then it is what is intended—God. The author then notes that all means that prepare for needs and necessities (possible reference to crafts or events) cannot achieve their end without terminating at the Necessary Existent. This is why the Quran says: "And that to your Lord is the final end" (Surah al-Najm 42). Whoever truly reflects recognizes that this word is the source of all goods and the center of benefits and happiness. The passage ends with a prayer: "With Allah is success."

Key Terms
واجب الوجود لذاته
ممكن الوجود
الدور
التسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument is circular because it assumes the necessary being at the start.
Correction: The argument does not assume a necessary being; it shows that any contingent agent, if posited, ultimately requires a necessary being to avoid circularity and infinite regress.

Checkpoint

B) It would need a cause, leading to infinite regress or circularity, which are invalid.
C) It would be a body, which is impossible.
D) It would be eternal and not need a creator.

Key Takeaway
Any contingent being demands a chain that must end with the Necessary Existent, as circularity and infinite regress are impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You saw that every contingent thing—including your own intellect, your soul, your very existence—depends on a Necessary Being. Do you live each moment aware of that dependence, or do you act as if you are self-sufficient? Today, before every action, pause and say: 'Without Allah, I cannot even take this breath.' Will you do that?
?
Al-Razi concluded that the word 'to your Lord is the final end' is the fountain of all goods. Is your heart truly anchored in God as your ultimate end, or are you chasing secondary goals—status, comfort, people—as if they were final? What would it mean for you to reorient one major pursuit today toward Allah alone?
?
The passage warns that infinite regress and circularity are impossible—there must be a stopping point. In your life, you may be stuck in cycles of seeking fulfillment in things that never satisfy. Are you willing to break that cycle by turning to the Necessary Existent, who alone can give lasting peace? What is one concrete step you can take right now to stop the regress?

Proof from Celestial Revolutions and Infinite Motions
Introduces proof from celestial motions for God's existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ancient philosophers' argument from the infinite motions of the celestial spheres to the existence of a non-corporeal Creator.

Core Idea
The heavens' endless motions demand a non-bodily, non-corporeal Agent.

This passage introduces a powerful argument for God's existence based on the celestial world's motions. The author contrasts it with a previous argument from the human body and explains why this one is stronger. By examining the cycles and motions of the heavens, the ancient philosophers concluded that their agent must be beyond physical limitations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the claim
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation. Notice that the author is presenting a new proof based on the celestial world.
The passage mentions a previous proof from the human body for comparison.
2
Understand the argument's logical steps
Break down the argument: cycles without end → motions without beginning/end → requires an agent → agent must be powerful over infinite acts → agent cannot be body/corporeal → therefore, a non-corporeal existent (Allah).
This is a chain of reasoning that moves from observed phenomena to a necessary conclusion.
3
Appreciate the scriptural support
Notice the Quranic verse quoted: 'The creation of the heavens and the earth is greater than the creation of people.' This reinforces the argument's strength.
The author uses revelation to support rational proof.
4
Note the premise structure
The author indicates that this proof is composed of premises, beginning with the first premise on establishing motions without beginning or end. This sets up further elaboration.
The text cuts off, but we see the beginning of the premise list.

الفصل الثالث والعشرون في إقامة الدلالة على وجود إله العالم بناء على جددت الصفات من طريق آخر اعلم أن الطريق الذي ذكرناه في الاستدلال بحدوث بدن الإنسان هو استدلال بحال من الأحوال. وههنا طريق شبيه به ولكنه استدلال بحال من أحوال عالم الأفلاك ، وهو العالم الأعلى . ومن المعلوم : أن الاستدلال بأحوال ذلك العالم على وجود الإله أظهر وأقوى . كما قال في الكتاب الإلهي : : لخلق السموات والأرض أكبر من خلق الناس . وهذا الطريق هو الذي كان يعول عليه قدماء الفلاسفة في إثبات الإله ، لهذا العالم . قالوا : حصل في هذا العالم أدوار لا نهاية لها ، وحركات لا أول لها ولا آخر ولا بد لها من فاعل ، وفاعلها يكون قوياً على أفعال لا نهاية لها ، وفاعل الأفعال التي لا نهاية لها ، يمتنع أن يكون جسماً أو جسمانياً ، فوجب الاعتراف بموجود ليس بجسم ولا بجماني ، وهو المحرك لهذه الأفعال ، والكواكب . وذلك الموجود هو الله تعالى . واعلم أن هذا الدليل مركب من مقدمات : المقدمة الأولى : في إثبات حركات لا أول لها ولا آخر لها . والحكماء عولوا
The twenty-third chapter: On establishing evidence for the existence of the God of the world based on [جددت الصفات] from another way. Know that the way which we mentioned in the proof by the temporality of the human body is a proof by a state among states. And here is a way similar to it, but it is a proof by a state of the states of the world of the celestial spheres, and it is the higher world. And it is known that the proof by the states of that world for the existence of God is more apparent and stronger. As He said in the divine book: 'The creation of the heavens and the earth is greater than the creation of people.' And this way is what the ancient philosophers relied upon in proving God for this world. They said: There occurred in this world cycles that have no end, and motions that have no beginning and no end, and they must have an agent, and their agent must be powerful over actions that have no end. And the agent of actions that have no end cannot be a body or corporeal. So it is necessary to acknowledge an existent that is not a body nor corporeal, and it is the mover of these actions and the planets. And that existent is Allah the Exalted. And know that this proof is composed of premises: The first premise: on proving motions that have no beginning and no end. And the philosophers relied...
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage begins a new chapter (the twenty-third) that presents a different argument for God's existence. The author contrasts it with a previous method based on the human body's temporality. The new method is based on the state of the celestial world (عالم الأفلاك), which is the higher world. The proof from this world is clearer and stronger, as the Quranic verse (Surah Ghafir 57) indicates: 'The creation of the heavens and the earth is greater than the creation of people.' This was the method of ancient philosophers. They argued that in this world there are cycles (adwar) without end, and motions without beginning or end. These require an agent. The agent must be powerful enough to perform infinite actions. Such an agent cannot be a body or corporeal (jismani). Therefore, one must acknowledge an existent that is neither body nor corporeal, which is the mover of these actions and the planets—that is Allah. The author then notes that this proof is composed of premises, and he begins listing them: the first premise establishes motions without beginning or end. The text cuts off while mentioning that the philosophers relied on something, but the content of that premise is not provided here.

The Philosophers' Proof for God from Celestial Motions
Philosophers' proof from eternal celestial motions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' argument for God's existence based on the eternal motions of the celestial sphere.

Core Idea
The endless motions of the heavens demand a non-corporeal mover, which is God.

The author presents a powerful argument from the celestial world, distinct from the earlier argument based on the human body. The vastness and continuity of celestial motions lead the philosophers to infer a non-material agent capable of infinite action. This lesson unpacks their reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Get a feel for the author's style.
Notice the Quranic citation (40:57) used to emphasize the strength of this argument.
2
Identify the three key premises
Find the statements about endless motions, the need for an agent, and the impossibility of the agent being a body.
These premises form the logical skeleton of the argument.
3
Understand why the agent cannot be a body
The text asserts that bodies can only produce finite effects, so an agent of infinite actions must be non-material. Reflect on why that is.
This is the crucial step that leads to transcendence.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The conclusion is that a non-corporeal existent—God—must be the mover of the celestial motions.
Note that this argument does not assert eternal creation, only a necessary mover.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم أن الطريق الذي ذكرناه في الاستدلال بحدوث بدن الإنسان هو استدلال بحال من الأحوال. وههنا طريق شبيه به ولكنه استدلال بحال من أحوال عالم الأفلاك، وهو العالم الأعلى. ومن المعلوم: أن الاستدلال بأحوال ذلك العالم على وجود الإله أظهر وأقوى. كما قال في الكتاب الإلهي: لخلق السموات والأرض أكبر من خلق الناس. وهذا الطريق هو الذي كان يعول عليه قدماء الفلاسفة في إثبات الإله لهذا العالم. قالوا: حصل في هذا العالم أدوار لا نهاية لها، وحركات لا أول لها ولا آخر ولا بد لها من فاعل، وفاعلها يكون قوياً على أفعال لا نهاية لها، وفاعل الأفعال التي لا نهاية لها، يمتنع أن يكون جسماً أو جسمانياً، فوجب الاعتراف بموجود ليس بجسم ولا بجسماني، وهو المحرك لهذه الأفعال والكواكب. وذلك الموجود هو الله تعالى.
Know that the method we mentioned in inferring from the temporality of the human body is an inference based on one state of affairs. Here there is a similar method, but it is an inference based on a state of affairs of the celestial world, which is the higher world. It is known that inference from the states of that world regarding the existence of God is clearer and stronger. As it is said in the divine book: 'The creation of the heavens and the earth is greater than the creation of mankind.' This method is the one upon which the ancient philosophers relied in establishing the existence of God for this world. Commentary
This passage presents the philosophers' argument for God's existence based on the celestial realm. The author first distinguishes this method from the previous one based on the human body, stating that this method is clearer and stronger, citing Quran 40:57. He then outlines the philosophers' reasoning: 1) The celestial world contains endless cycles and motions with no beginning or end. 2) These motions require an agent capable of performing infinite actions. 3) Such an agent cannot be a body or corporeal, because bodies can only produce finite effects. 4) Therefore, there must exist a non-corporeal, non-material mover, which is God. The argument thus infers the existence of a transcendent divine being from the observed continuity of celestial motions.

The First Premise: Eternal Motions Without Beginning or End
Analysis of the first premise with two formulations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the philosophers sought to prove the existence of eternal motions through the nature of time, and how the author reformulated the argument based on causation.

Core Idea
Eternal motions are deduced from the impossibility of a first cause without a condition.

Before we can consider the proof for God's existence, we must understand the premise that there are motions with no beginning or end. The philosophers argued this from time itself, but the author presents an alternative path that avoids relying on time. This lesson unpacks that first premise in detail.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two parts of the first premise
Recognize that the first premise has two formulations: the philosophers' original method using time, and the author's alternative method based on causation.
The premise aims to prove motions with no first or last.
2
Understand the philosophers' original argument
The philosophers argue that time is the measure of motion, and since time cannot have a beginning or end, motion must also be eternal.
This relies on the nature of time as a measure.
3
Follow the author's alternative chain of reasoning
The author starts from a temporal event, considers its cause (eternal or temporal), and shows that an unconditioned eternal cause is impossible, leading to a chain of temporal causes without beginning.
The alternative argument avoids depending on time's nature.
4
See how the conclusion of eternal motions is reached
The chain of temporal causes cannot proceed infinitely at once, so it must be an infinite succession without a first—exactly what the philosophers affirm: eternal motions.
This establishes the first premise for the subsequent proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن هذا الدليل مركب من مقدمات: المقدمة الأولى: في إثبات حركات لا أول لها ولا آخر لها. والحكماء عولوا في إثبات هذا المطلوب على أن الزمان مقدار الحركة، ثم ثبت أن الزمان يمتنع أن يحصل له أول وآخر فوجب الاعتراف بوجود حركة لا أول لها ولا آخر لها. ومقدمات هذه الحجة مشهورة. وقال المصنف رحمة الله عليه: وعندي أنه يمكن تقريره بطريق آخر بناء على أصول الفلاسفة، فيقال: لا شك أن ههنا حركات وتغييرات، فهذه الحوادث لا بد لها من سبب، وسبب هذا الحادث إما أن يكون قديماً أو حادثاً. فإن كان قديماً فإما أن يتوقف إلحاقه لهذا الحادث على شرط أو لا يتوقف. فإن لم يتوقف فحينئذ قد كان هذا القديم موجوداً من الأزل إلى الآن من غير صدور هذا الحادث عنه ثم صدر هذا الحادث من غير أن يتميز هذا الوقت عن سائر الأوقات بما لأجله صار أولى بحدوث هذا الحادث، وهذا يقتضي رجحان الممكن لا لمرجح وهو محال. فثبت أن بتقدير أن يكون السبب المؤثر في حدوث هذا الحادث موجوداً قديماً، إلا أنه يجب الاعتراف بأن تأثيره في وجود هذا الحادث مشروط بشرط حادث، فحينئذ يرجح الأمر إلى القسم الثاني وهو أن الأثر الحادث لابد له من سبب حادث. ثم الكلام في ذلك الحادث كالكلام في الأول فيفضي هذا إلى التسلسل، وإما أن يحصل التسلسل في أسباب ومسببات توجد دفعة واحدة وهو محال، وإما أن لا يحصل بحيث يكون كل واحد منها مسبوقاً بآخر لا إلى أول، وذلك هو الذي تقول به الفلاسفة ويذهبون إليه. وعند ظهور هذا المعنى قد ثبت لهم وجود حوادث لا أول لها، ووجود حركات لا بداية لها. وأما المقدمة الثانية: وهي قولهم هذه الحوادث لابد لها من مؤثر وفاعل وموجد فتقرير هذه المقدمة مبني على أن الجسم يمتنع أن يتحرك لنفسه أو لذاته، والكلام في هذه المسألة مذكور في العلم الطبيعي على سبيل
Know that this proof is composed of premises: The first premise: establishing motions with no beginning and no end. The philosophers relied in establishing this desired conclusion on the fact that time is the measure of motion, then it is established that time is impossible to have a beginning and an end, so it is necessary to acknowledge the existence of motion with no beginning and no end. The premises of this argument are well-known. The author, may God have mercy on him, said: In my view, it can be formulated in another way based on the principles of the philosophers, so it is said: There is no doubt that here there are motions and changes, so these temporal events must have a cause, and the cause of this temporal event is either eternal or temporal. If it is eternal, then either its bringing about of this temporal event depends on a condition or it does not. If it does not, then this eternal being would have existed from eternity until now without this event occurring from it, then this event occurs without this time being distinguished from other times by something that makes it more appropriate for the occurrence of this event, and this necessitates the preponderance of a possible without a preponderator, which is impossible. So it is established that, assuming the effective cause of the occurrence of this temporal event is an eternal existent, yet it must be acknowledged that its effect in the existence of this temporal event is conditional upon a temporal condition. Then the matter leads to the second division, which is that the temporal effect must have a temporal cause. Then the discussion about that temporal cause is like the discussion about the first, leading to infinite regress. Either there is an infinite regress in causes and effects that occur at once, which is impossible, or there is not, such that each of them is preceded by another without first, and that is what the philosophers say and hold. Upon the emergence of this meaning, they have established the existence of events with no beginning, and motions with no starting point. As for the second premise: which is their statement that these events must have an effecter, agent, and bringer into existence. The formulation of this premise is based on the fact that a body is impossible to move by itself or by its essence. The discussion of this issue is mentioned in natural science in the way...
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is an analysis of the philosophers' proof into two premises. The first premise aims to establish the existence of motions with no beginning or end. The author first presents the philosophers' own method: they argue that time is the measure of motion, and since time cannot have a beginning or end, motion must also be eternal. He then offers his own alternative formulation, which avoids relying on the nature of time. His reasoning proceeds by considering a temporal event: it must have a cause, which is either eternal or temporal. If the cause is eternal and unconditioned, the temporal event would have occurred eternally, but it does not, so there must be a temporal condition. This leads to a chain of temporal causes, which either results in an infinite regress (which is impossible if all occur simultaneously) or a chain without a first cause — which is exactly what the philosophers affirm. Thus, from the impossibility of an eternal cause without condition, the philosophers deduce a series of temporal causes without beginning, i.e., eternal motions. The second premise (stated briefly at the end) is that such motions require an agent, and this is based on the principle that a body cannot move itself — a topic from natural science.

الزمان
مقدار الحركة
التسلسل
السبب الحادث
القديم
الممكن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author rejects the philosophers' conclusion that motions are eternal.
Correction: The author provides an alternative formulation to establish the same conclusion; he does not reject it.

Checkpoint
In the author's alternative formulation, what is the consequence of assuming an eternal cause that does not depend on any condition for producing a temporal effect?
A) The cause would produce the effect eternally
B) The effect would occur without a cause
C) The cause would be temporal
D) The effect would be impossible

Key Takeaway
The first premise establishes eternal motions by showing that temporal events require an infinite chain of causes without a first cause.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every change in your life is part of an infinite chain of causes, does that make you feel less responsible for your actions, or does it drive you to seek the ultimate Cause of your existence?
?
The argument shows that an eternal cause can produce temporal effects only through a condition. What condition in your life allows the eternal God to change your heart? Are you placing yourself under that condition?
?
You admit the world is filled with change and motion. But have you ever paused to think that the very fact that you exist right now requires a cause beyond the infinite chain? What is that cause to you personally?

The Second Premise: Events Need an Agent
Brief statement of the second premise and its basis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second premise of the philosopher's proof: that eternal motions require an external agent, and a body cannot move itself.

Core Idea
Every motion needs a mover; a body cannot move itself.

Having established that there are eternal motions, the philosophers now argue that such motions must have an efficient cause. This second premise is based on a fundamental principle of natural philosophy: a body does not move by its own essence. This lesson covers that crucial point, though the text is cut short.

Guided Path
1
Read the brief statement of the second premise
The author says the second premise is that these events require an effecter, agent, and bringer into existence. Read the Arabic and translation.
The passage ends mid-sentence, but the main idea is clear.
2
Understand the underlying principle
The principle is that a body cannot move by itself or by its essence. This is discussed in natural science.
This principle is used to argue that motion requires an external mover.
3
Connect this premise to the overall proof
Together with the first premise (eternal motions), this premise leads to the conclusion that there must be an eternal agent that causes these motions.
This sets up the need for a necessary being.

Corporeal Powers Are Essentially Finite
Proof that corporeal power is finite via divisibility and part-analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why any corporeal power cannot produce infinite actions, based on the divisibility of its substrate and an analysis of its parts.

Core Idea
Corporeal power is divisible, so its action must be finite.

This lesson examines the third premise in the proof of a non-corporeal mover: that corporeal power is limited to finite actions. The argument proceeds from the fact that corporeal power inheres in a divisible substrate. By analyzing the possible capacities of a part of that power, the author demonstrates that only finite actions can result.

Guided Path
1
Understand the divisibility claim
Every corporeal power is an accident in a spatially extended substrate, which is divisible. Hence the power itself is divisible.
This relies on denying the indivisible atom.
2
Consider the three possibilities for a part
A part of the power either has no power, equal power to the whole, or less power than the whole. Each must be examined.
3
Recognize that each leads to finitude
The first two are contradictory; the third implies the whole's action is a finite multiple of the part's finite action.
Thus the whole's action is finite.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المقدمة الثالثة: فهي بيان أن القوة الجسمانية لا تقوى على أفعال غير متناهية، وتقرير هذه المقدمة: أن كل قوة جسمانية فهي حالة في محل متحيز. وكل متحيز منقسم، بناء على نفي الجوهر الفرد، وكل ما كان حالا في محل منقسم فهو منقسم، وكل قوة جسمانية فهي منقسمة. إذا ثبت هذا فنقول جزء تلك القوة إما أن لا يقوى على شيء أصلا، أو يقوى عليه الكل، أو يقوى على شيء أنقص مما يقوى عليه الكل، والأقسام الثلاثة باطلة. وإنما قلنا: إنه يستحيل أن يقال: إن جزء القوة لا يقوى على شيء أصلاً لأن تلك القوة ليس إلا تلك الأجزاء ولا يقوى على شيء أصلاً فوجب أن يقال: إن مجموع تلك القوة لا تقوى على شيء أصلا، فيلزم أن يقال: إن القوة على الشيء، ليست قوة على الشيء. هذا خلف. وأما القسم الثاني: وهو أن يقال: إن جزء القوة يقوي على تمام ما تقوى عليه كل القوة فهذا أيضاً محال لأنه يلزم أن يكون الكل مثل الجزء من غير تفاوت أصلاً، وذلك محال. وأما الثالث: وهو أن يقال: إن جزء القوة يقوى على بعض ما يقوى عليه الكل. فنقول: إذا كان الأمر كذلك، فإذا فرضنا أن كل تلك القوة وجزءها أخذا في التحريك من مبدأ معين، فحينئذ يلزم أن يتناهي فعل الجزء، وإذا كان كذلك ففعل الكل يكون أضعاف فعل الجزء بمرات متناهية، وأضعاف المتناهي متناهي، فوجب أن يكون فعل القوة متناهياً، فثبت أن القوى الجسمانية يجب أن تكون أفعالها متناهية، ويمتنع صدور أفعال غير متناهية عن القوة الجسمانية. فقد ظهر من هذا الوجه صحة هذه المقدمات. وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول: ثبت بالدليل وجود حركات غير متناهية، وثبت بالدليل أنه لا بد لها من مؤثر يؤثر فيها، ومن موجد يوجدها، وثبت بالدليل أن موجد الأفعال الغير متناهية يمتنع أن يكون جسماً أو جسمانياً فلم يبق إلا الاعتراف بوجود موجود ليس بجسم ولا بجسماني، وهو المحرك لأجرام الأفلاك والكواكب، وهو المحرك للعناصر بحسب امتزاجاتها التي لا بداية لها، وذلك الموجود هو إله العالم ومدبر العالم. وهذه الطريقة كان قدماء الفلاسفة من أصحاب أرسطاطاليس يعولون عليها في إثبات الإله لهذا العالم.
As for the third premise: it is an explanation that corporeal power (al-quwwa al-jismāniyya) does not have power over infinite actions. The exposition of this premise: every corporeal power is an accident in a spatially extended substrate. And every spatially extended substrate is divisible, based on the denial of the indivisible atom. And everything that is an accident in a divisible substrate is divisible. So every corporeal power is divisible. If this is established, we say: a part of that power either has no power over anything at all, or has power over the whole, or has power over something less than that over which the whole has power. All three divisions are invalid. We say: it is impossible to say that a part of the power has no power over anything at all, because that power is nothing but those parts, and if a part has no power over anything at all, then it must be said that the sum of that power has no power over anything at all. Consequently, it would be said that the power over a thing is not a power over a thing. This is a contradiction. As for the second division: that a part of the power is powerful over the entirety of what the whole power is powerful over — this also is impossible, because it would necessitate that the whole is like the part without any difference at all, and that is impossible. As for the third: that a part of the power is powerful over some of what the whole is powerful over. We say: if that is the case, then if we suppose that the entire power and its part begin to move from a given starting point, then it necessarily follows that the action of the part is finite. And if that is the case, then the action of the whole would be multiples of the action of the part by finite amounts, and multiples of the finite are finite. So it must be that the action of the power is finite. Thus it is established that corporeal powers must have finite actions, and it is impossible for infinite actions to issue from a corporeal power. So from this aspect the validity of these premises has become clear. And if this is established, we say: it has been proven by evidence that there exist infinite motions; it has been proven by evidence that they must have an agent that effects them, and a bringer-into-existence that brings them into existence; and it has been proven by evidence that the bringer-into-existence of infinite actions cannot be a body or corporeal. So nothing remains but to acknowledge the existence of an existent that is not a body and not corporeal, and He is the mover of the celestial bodies and planets, and He is the mover of the elements according to their mixtures that have no beginning. That existent is the God of the world and the Governor of the world. And this method was relied upon by the ancient philosophers, the followers of Aristotle, in proving the God of this world.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage presents a proof that corporeal power cannot produce infinite actions, leading to the conclusion that the mover of infinite motions must be non-corporeal, i.e., God. The passage first states the third premise: corporeal power (al-quwwa al-jismāniyya) is incapable of infinite actions. The author then explains this premise by noting that every corporeal power is an accident (hāl) in a spatially extended substrate (maḥall mutaḥayyiz). Every spatially extended substrate is divisible (munqasim), based on the denial of the indivisible atom (jawhar fard). Hence, since the power inheres in a divisible substrate, it is itself divisible. With divisibility established, the author examines three possibilities for a part of that power: (1) the part has no power at all; (2) the part has power equal to the whole; (3) the part has power less than the whole. Each is shown to be impossible. For the first, if a part has no power, the sum (the whole) would also have no power, contradicting the fact that it does have power. For the second, if a part equals the whole, there would be no distinction between part and whole, which is absurd. For the third, if a part has power over a portion, then when the whole and part begin to act from a starting point, the part's action will be finite; the whole's action would be a finite multiple of that, hence also finite. Thus the whole's action must be finite. The passage then concludes: since it has been established that there are infinite motions (by separate proof), their agent cannot be corporeal; it must be a non-corporeal existent, which is the mover of celestial bodies and elements—God. The author notes that this was the method of the ancient Peripatetics.

Key Terms
القوة الجسمانية
المتحيز
الجوهر الفرد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that a part of a corporeal power could have zero power without affecting the whole's power.
Correction: The author argues that if all parts have zero power, the sum cannot have power, so the part must have some power.

Checkpoint
Why does the author rule out the possibility that a part of corporeal power has power equal to the whole?
A) Because it would imply the whole has no power.
B) Because it would imply the whole is not greater than the part, which is absurd.
C) Because the part cannot move anything.
D) Because the power is indivisible.

Key Takeaway
All corporeal powers are finite because their divisibility forces any part to produce only finite actions, and the whole's action is a finite multiple of that.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every physical power you possess is inherently finite, where do you truly place your trust for the things that matter most—your health, your provision, your lasting impact? Does your daily routine reflect reliance on your own limited strength or on the Infinite Power of Allah? Name one area where you have been acting as if your power is unlimited and commit to surrendering it to Allah today.
?
The proof shows that even the sum of all corporeal powers is finite. What hope is there for any lasting success that does not rely on the Creator? Consider something you are striving for right now. How does the finitude of your own ability change the way you approach that goal, and what step can you take to anchor your hope in Allah rather than yourself?

From Infinite Motions to a Non-Corporeal Mover
Conclusion from finitude of corporeal power to a non-corporeal mover for infinite motions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the finitude of corporeal power leads to the conclusion that the mover of infinite motions must be non-corporeal, i.e., God.

Core Idea
Infinite motions require a non-corporeal mover.

Building on the established premise that corporeal powers can only produce finite actions, this lesson applies it to the existence of infinite motions (proven elsewhere). Since the agent of such infinite motions cannot be corporeal, it must be a non-bodily existent — the First Mover, God. The passage also notes that this was the approach of the Peripatetic philosophers.

Guided Path
1
Recall the finitude of corporeal power
Remember from the previous lesson that any corporeal power can only produce finite actions.
2
Acknowledge the existence of infinite motions
The author states it has been proven elsewhere that there are infinite motions (e.g., celestial rotations).
This is taken as given in this argument.
3
Draw the conclusion
Since the agent of these infinite motions cannot be corporeal (otherwise its power would be finite), it must be a non-corporeal being—God.
This non-corporeal mover is the First Mover of the universe.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المقدمة الثالثة: فهي بيان أن القوة الجسمانية لا تقوى على أفعال غير متناهية، وتقرير هذه المقدمة: أن كل قوة جسمانية فهي حالة في محل متحيز. وكل متحيز منقسم، بناء على نفي الجوهر الفرد، وكل ما كان حالا في محل منقسم فهو منقسم، وكل قوة جسمانية فهي منقسمة. إذا ثبت هذا فنقول جزء تلك القوة إما أن لا يقوى على شيء أصلا، أو يقوى عليه الكل، أو يقوى على شيء أنقص مما يقوى عليه الكل، والأقسام الثلاثة باطلة. وإنما قلنا: إنه يستحيل أن يقال: إن جزء القوة لا يقوى على شيء أصلاً لأن تلك القوة ليس إلا تلك الأجزاء ولا يقوى على شيء أصلاً فوجب أن يقال: إن مجموع تلك القوة لا تقوى على شيء أصلا، فيلزم أن يقال: إن القوة على الشيء، ليست قوة على الشيء. هذا خلف. وأما القسم الثاني: وهو أن يقال: إن جزء القوة يقوي على تمام ما تقوى عليه كل القوة فهذا أيضاً محال لأنه يلزم أن يكون الكل مثل الجزء من غير تفاوت أصلاً، وذلك محال. وأما الثالث: وهو أن يقال: إن جزء القوة يقوى على بعض ما يقوى عليه الكل. فنقول: إذا كان الأمر كذلك، فإذا فرضنا أن كل تلك القوة وجزءها أخذا في التحريك من مبدأ معين، فحينئذ يلزم أن يتناهي فعل الجزء، وإذا كان كذلك ففعل الكل يكون أضعاف فعل الجزء بمرات متناهية، وأضعاف المتناهي متناهي، فوجب أن يكون فعل القوة متناهياً، فثبت أن القوى الجسمانية يجب أن تكون أفعالها متناهية، ويمتنع صدور أفعال غير متناهية عن القوة الجسمانية. فقد ظهر من هذا الوجه صحة هذه المقدمات. وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول: ثبت بالدليل وجود حركات غير متناهية، وثبت بالدليل أنه لا بد لها من مؤثر يؤثر فيها، ومن موجد يوجدها، وثبت بالدليل أن موجد الأفعال الغير متناهية يمتنع أن يكون جسماً أو جسمانياً فلم يبق إلا الاعتراف بوجود موجود ليس بجسم ولا بجسماني، وهو المحرك لأجرام الأفلاك والكواكب، وهو المحرك للعناصر بحسب امتزاجاتها التي لا بداية لها، وذلك الموجود هو إله العالم ومدبر العالم. وهذه الطريقة كان قدماء الفلاسفة من أصحاب أرسطاطاليس يعولون عليها في إثبات الإله لهذا العالم.
As for the third premise: it is an explanation that corporeal power (al-quwwa al-jismāniyya) does not have power over infinite actions. The exposition of this premise: every corporeal power is an accident in a spatially extended substrate. And every spatially extended substrate is divisible, based on the denial of the indivisible atom. And everything that is an accident in a divisible substrate is divisible. So every corporeal power is divisible. If this is established, we say: a part of that power either has no power over anything at all, or has power over the whole, or has power over something less than that over which the whole has power. All three divisions are invalid. We say: it is impossible to say that a part of the power has no power over anything at all, because that power is nothing but those parts, and if a part has no power over anything at all, then it must be said that the sum of that power has no power over anything at all. Consequently, it would be said that the power over a thing is not a power over a thing. This is a contradiction. As for the second division: that a part of the power is powerful over the entirety of what the whole power is powerful over — this also is impossible, because it would necessitate that the whole is like the part without any difference at all, and that is impossible. As for the third: that a part of the power is powerful over some of what the whole is powerful over. We say: if that is the case, then if we suppose that the entire power and its part begin to move from a given starting point, then it necessarily follows that the action of the part is finite. And if that is the case, then the action of the whole would be multiples of the action of the part by finite amounts, and multiples of the finite are finite. So it must be that the action of the power is finite. Thus it is established that corporeal powers must have finite actions, and it is impossible for infinite actions to issue from a corporeal power. So from this aspect the validity of these premises has become clear. And if this is established, we say: it has been proven by evidence that there exist infinite motions; it has been proven by evidence that they must have an agent that effects them, and a bringer-into-existence that brings them into existence; and it has been proven by evidence that the bringer-into-existence of infinite actions cannot be a body or corporeal. So nothing remains but to acknowledge the existence of an existent that is not a body and not corporeal, and He is the mover of the celestial bodies and planets, and He is the mover of the elements according to their mixtures that have no beginning. That existent is the God of the world and the Governor of the world. And this method was relied upon by the ancient philosophers, the followers of Aristotle, in proving the God of this world.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage presents a proof that corporeal power cannot produce infinite actions, leading to the conclusion that the mover of infinite motions must be non-corporeal, i.e., God. The passage first states the third premise: corporeal power (al-quwwa al-jismāniyya) is incapable of infinite actions. The author then explains this premise by noting that every corporeal power is an accident (hāl) in a spatially extended substrate (maḥall mutaḥayyiz). Every spatially extended substrate is divisible (munqasim), based on the denial of the indivisible atom (jawhar fard). Hence, since the power inheres in a divisible substrate, it is itself divisible. With divisibility established, the author examines three possibilities for a part of that power: (1) the part has no power at all; (2) the part has power equal to the whole; (3) the part has power less than the whole. Each is shown to be impossible. For the first, if a part has no power, the sum (the whole) would also have no power, contradicting the fact that it does have power. For the second, if a part equals the whole, there would be no distinction between part and whole, which is absurd. For the third, if a part has power over a portion, then when the whole and part begin to act from a starting point, the part's action will be finite; the whole's action would be a finite multiple of that, hence also finite. Thus the whole's action must be finite. The passage then concludes: since it has been established that there are infinite motions (by separate proof), their agent cannot be corporeal; it must be a non-corporeal existent, which is the mover of celestial bodies and elements—God. The author notes that this was the method of the ancient Peripatetics.

Key Terms
الحركات غير المتناهية
جسماني

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that an infinite chain of corporeal movers could explain infinite motions.
Correction: The author argues that each corporeal mover would have finite power, so even an infinite chain would not produce an infinite effect; the first mover must be non-corporeal.

Checkpoint

D) Because bodies are divisible.

Key Takeaway
The existence of infinite motions in the universe demands a non-corporeal mover, which is God, as argued by the Peripatetic philosophers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Do you live as though matter is all there is? What would it mean to live with the awareness that a non-corporeal God is constantly sustaining every motion of the universe? Will you tonight reflect on one motion in your life—a thought, a heartbeat, the rotation of the earth—and consciously attribute it to that Mover?

The author says this proof was relied upon by ancient philosophers. Have you ever felt that intellectual arguments for God are just for scholars? This passage was given to you. What excuse do you have now to not let this proof settle in your heart? Will you memorize the three key premises today so that they become part of your conviction?

If you truly accept that He governs every motion, why do you still worry about the outcomes of your own small motions? Are you trusting your own finite power more than His infinite agency? Why Motion Cannot Be Eternal
The mutakallimun argue that motion must have a first beginning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the mutakallimun's proof that motion must have a first beginning, based on the contradiction between the essence of motion and the concept of eternity.

Core Idea
Motion's essence demands a beginning; eternity denies one, so eternal motion is impossible.

In this passage, the author presents a concise proof from the mutakallimun that motion must have a first beginning. By analyzing the very nature of motion and the meaning of eternity, they show that eternal motion leads to a logical contradiction. This argument is foundational for establishing that the universe had a beginning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice how the argument builds from definitions to a contradiction.
The passage ends mid-sentence; focus on the complete argument given.
2
Identify the two definitions
The passage defines motion as 'transition from state to state' and eternity as 'negation of firstness'. Understand the implications of each definition.
Motion's definition implies being preceded; eternity's definition implies not being preceded.
3
Understand the contradiction
If we suppose eternal motion, it would have to be both preceded (as motion) and not preceded (as eternal). This is impossible, so eternal motion cannot exist.
Thus, motion must have a first moment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن مذهب المتكلمين: أن القول بوجود حوادث لا أول لها محال، وأنه يجب انتهاء الحوادث إلى حادث هو أول الحوادث. ودلائلهم كثيرة سنذكرها في مسألة الحدوث والقدم. إلا أنا نذكر ههنا واحداً من تلك الدلائل، فنقول: إن الدليل على أن الأمر كما ذكرناه: أن ماهية الحركة وحقيقتها: أنها من حالة إلى حالة، وكل ما كان كذلك فإن حقيقته تقتضي أن يكون مسبوقاً بالحالة المنتقل عنها، وكل ما كان كذلك، فإن حقيقته تقتضي تكون مسبوقة بغيرها، فثبت أن حقيقة الحركة وماهيتها تقتضي أن تكون مسبوقة بغيرها. وأما حقيقة الأزل ونفي الأولية فهي تقتضي أن لا تكون مسبوقة بغيرها، وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول: لو فرضنا حركة موجودة في الأزل، فهي لكونها حركة إما أن تكون مسبوقة بغيرها، أو لكونها أزلية يجب أن لا تكون مسبوقة بغيرها. وذلك يوجب الجمع بين النقيضين، وهو محال. فيثبت بهذا البرهان: أنه لا بد للحركات من أول، ومن بداية، وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول: إنه قبل ذلك الوقت الذي هو أول الحركات، إما أن يقال: كانت
Know that the doctrine of the mutakallimūn is that the statement that there exist events without a beginning is impossible, and that events must terminate at an event that is the first of events. Their proofs are many, which we will mention in the issue of origination and eternity. But here we mention one of those proofs. We say: the proof that the matter is as we have stated is that the essence (māhiyya) of motion and its reality is that it is from a state to a state, and everything that is like that, its reality necessitates that it be preceded by the state from which it leaves; and everything that is like that, its reality necessitates that it be preceded by something else. So it is established that the reality and essence of motion necessitate that it be preceded by something else. As for the reality of eternity (al-azal) and the negation of firstness, it necessitates that it not be preceded by something else. And if this is established, we say: if we suppose a motion existing in eternity, then because it is a motion, it must be preceded by something else, or because it is eternal, it must not be preceded by something else. That necessitates combining two opposites, which is impossible. So by this proof it is established that motions must have a first and a beginning. And if this is established, we say: before that time which is the first of motions, either it is said that it was...
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage presents the mutakallimūn's argument that motion cannot be eternal; rather, it must have a first beginning. The author first states the doctrine: events (hawādith) cannot be beginningless; they must terminate at a first event. Then he gives one proof: The essence of motion is to be a transition from one state to another. Therefore, by its very nature, motion is preceded by the state from which it departs, and thus it is preceded by something else. In contrast, the essence of eternity (al-azal) and the negation of firstness require that it not be preceded. If we suppose a motion existing in eternity, it would simultaneously require precedence (because it is motion) and non-precedence (because it is eternal). This is a contradiction. Hence, motion cannot be eternal, and there must be a first motion. The passage then begins to conclude that before that first motion, there must be a state (likely rest or the Creator's power), but the text cuts off.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Eternal motion is possible if we consider time to be infinite and motion continuous.
Correction: The argument shows that motion's essence requires a prior state, regardless of time. An eternal motion would have no prior state, contradicting its own definition.

Key Takeaway
The mutakallimun prove that motion must have a first beginning because its essence requires a prior state, while eternity precludes any prior, making eternal motion contradictory.

Philosophical Proof of a Non-Corporeal Mover from Infinite Motions
Philosophical proof for a non-corporeal mover from infinite motions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the ancient philosophers proved the existence of a non-corporeal God by reasoning from the existence of infinite motions.

Core Idea
Infinite motions require a non-corporeal mover.

This lesson presents a classical philosophical proof for God's existence, often associated with Aristotle and his followers. The argument starts from the observation that there are infinite motions in the universe, and reasons that their ultimate cause cannot be a body or corporeal substance. We will walk through each step of the proof and see how it leads to affirming a non-corporeal creator and director of the world.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation once. Allow the author's flow to be heard before you analyse it.
2
Identify the three premises
The argument relies on three established premises. Find each one in the passage: existence of infinite motions, necessity of a cause, and impossibility of a corporeal cause.
The phrase 'thabata bil-dalil' marks each premise.
3
Understand why the mover cannot be corporeal
The passage asserts that the creator of infinite actions cannot be a body or corporeal. Think about why: bodies are limited and finite, so they cannot be the source of infinite effects.
This is a key inference in the proof.
4
See how this leads to the God of the world
After concluding that the mover is non-corporeal, the passage identifies this being as the mover of the spheres and planets and the director of the elements. That being is God.
The conclusion ties the philosophical argument to Islamic theology.
5
Reflect on historical context
The passage notes that this method was relied upon by the ancient philosophers, followers of Aristotle. Consider why this proof was important in their system.
This helps understand the broader philosophical tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول: ثبت بالدليل وجود حركات غير متناهية، وثبت بالدليل أنه لا بد لها من مؤثر يؤثر فيها، ومن موجد يوجدها، وثبت بالدليل أن موجد الأفعال الغير متناهية يمتنع أن يكون جسماً أو جسمانياً فلم يبق إلا الاعتراف بوجود موجود ليس بجسم ولا بجسماني، وهو المحرك لأجرام الأفلاك والكواكب، وهو المحرك للعناصر بحسب امتزاجاتها التي لا بداية لها، وذلك الموجود هو إله العالم ومدبر العالم. وهذه الطريقة كان قدماء الفلاسفة من أصحاب أرسطاطا ليس يعولون عليها في إثبات الإله لهذا العالم
And when this is established, we say: It is established by proof that there exist infinite motions, and it is established by proof that they must have an efficient cause that influences them and a creator that creates them, and it is established by proof that the creator of infinite actions cannot be a body or corporeal, so nothing remains except to acknowledge the existence of an existent that is not a body nor corporeal, and He is the mover of the spheres and planets, and He is the mover of the elements according to their endless blendings, and that existent is the God of the world and the Director of the world. And this method was relied upon by the ancient philosophers among the followers of Aristotle in proving the God for this world.

Commentary
This passage is a proof. The author first states that the premises have been established (referring to earlier arguments). Then he presents the philosophical argument: (1) It is proven that infinite motions exist. (2) These motions must have an efficient cause (mu'aththir) and a creator (mujid). (3) The creator of infinite acts cannot be a body (jism) or corporeal (jismani), because bodily things are limited. (4) Therefore, we must acknowledge a being that is neither body nor corporeal. This being is the mover of the celestial spheres and planets, and the mover of the elements in their never-ending combinations. That being is the God of the world and its Director. The author notes that the ancient philosophers, particularly followers of Aristotle, relied on this method to prove God's existence.

The Proof that Motion Must Have a First Beginning
The mutakallimun's proof that motion cannot be eternal due to contradiction between the essence of motion and pre-eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the mutakallimun's proof that motion cannot be eternal because its essence requires being preceded, which contradicts the nature of pre-eternity.

Core Idea
Motion's essence demands a before; pre-eternity forbids a before; therefore eternal motion is impossible.

The mutakallimun argue that all events must have a first event. Their central proof focuses on the nature of motion itself. By examining what motion is—a transition from one state to another—they show that eternal motion leads to a logical contradiction. This lesson unpacks that proof.

Guided Path
1
Understand the mutakallimun's position
The mutakallimun hold that events cannot regress infinitely; there must be a first event. Read the opening statement carefully.
This is the claim to be proven.
2
Analyze the essence of motion
The proof defines motion as a transition from one state to another. Notice that this definition implies that any motion must be preceded by the state it leaves.
3
Contrast with pre-eternity
Pre-eternity (al-azal) means having no beginning. If motion were eternal, it would have to be both preceded (as motion) and not preceded (as eternal), a contradiction.
This is the key step.
4
Conclude the proof
Since the combination of contradictories is impossible, eternal motion cannot exist. Therefore, motions must have a first beginning.
The proof is complete.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

فنقول: إنه قبل ذلك الوقت الذي هو أول الحركات، إما أن يقال: كانت الأجسام بأسرها معدومة ثم وجدت وتحركت، أو يقال: الأجسام وإن كانت موجودة إلا أنها كانت واقفة ساكنة، فلما جاء ذلك الوقت أحدث في حركاتها السريعة، بعضها إلى المشرق وبعضها إلى الغرب، وبعضها إلى الشمال، وبعضها إلى الجنوب. وعلى كلا التقديرين تصريح العقل يشهد بافتقارها إلى إله يحركها ويديرها. وأما إن قلنا: إنها كانت معدومة محضة ثم وجدت وتحركت، فالعقل يقضي بافتقارها إلى الموجد، وأما إن قلنا: إنها كانت موجودة، ولكنها كانت واقفة ثم ابتدأت من ذلك الوقت بالحركة فإن العقل يقضي بافتقارها إلى المحرك والمدير، فثبت أن حركات الأفلاك تدل على جميع الاعتبارات، على افتقارها إلى مدير يدبرها ومحرك يحركها. واعلم أن الفلاسفة قالوا: حركات الأفلاك لا أول لها، فوجب افتقارها إلى محرك يحركها، ومدير يدبرها والمتكلمون قالوا: حركات الأفلاك لها أول. فوجب افتقارها إلى محرك ومدبر. ويمكن أيضاً أن يقال: هذه الحركات إما أن يقال: إنه لا أول لها، وإما أن يقال: لها أول أيضاً فإن قلنا: إنه لا أول لها وجب افتقارها إلى الإله الذي ليس بجسم ولا بجسماني بالطريق الذي ذكره الفلاسفة، وإن قلنا: إن تلك الحركات لها بداية، ولها أول، وجب أيضاً افتقارها إلى المؤثر المحرك بالطريق الذي ذكره المتكلمون فظهر أن على جميع التقديرات لابد من الاعتراف بوجود إله لهذا العالم يبدبره ويتصرف فيه كيف شاء وأراد: (ألا له الخلق والأمر تبارك الله رب العالمين) وبالله التوفيق
And know that the doctrine of the mutakallimun is that the statement that there are events without a beginning is impossible, and that events must end at an event that is the first of events. And their proofs are many; we will mention them in the question of origination and pre-eternity. However, we mention here one of those proofs. We say: The proof that the matter is as we have mentioned is that the essence and reality of motion is that it is from a state to a state, and everything that is thus, its reality requires that it be preceded by the state from which it departs, and everything that is thus, its reality requires that it be preceded by something else. So it is established that the reality and essence of motion require that it be preceded by something else. As for the reality of pre-eternity and the negation of beginning, it requires that it not be preceded by something else. And when this is established, we say: If we suppose a motion existing in pre-eternity, then because it is motion it must be preceded by something else, or because it is pre-eternal it must not be preceded by something else. That necessitates combining two contradictories, which is impossible. So it is proven by this demonstration that motions must have a first and a beginning. And when this is established, we say: Before that time which is the first of motions, either it is said that all bodies were non-existent then came to be and moved, or it is said that bodies, though existent, were stationary and still, then when that time came, He caused in them rapid motions, some to the east, some to the west, some to the north, some to the south. In both cases, the pronouncement of reason bears witness to their need for a God who moves and directs them. And if we say that they were pure non-existence then came to be and moved, reason judges their need for a creator. And if we say that they were existent but stationary then began from that time to move, reason judges their need for a mover and director. So it is established that the motions of the spheres indicate in all respects their need for a director who directs them and a mover who moves them. Know that the philosophers said: The motions of the spheres have no beginning, so they must need a mover to move them and a director to direct them. The mutakallimun said: The motions of the spheres have a beginning, so they must need a mover and a director. And it can also be said: These motions are either said to have no beginning or said to have a beginning. If we say they have no beginning, they need the God who is neither a body nor corporeal by the method the philosophers mentioned. And if we say those motions have a beginning and a first, they also need the influential mover by the method the mutakallimun mentioned. So it appears that in all cases one must acknowledge the existence of a God for this world who directs it and disposes in it as He wills: 'Verily, His is the creation and the command; blessed is Allah, Lord of the worlds' (al-A'raf 7:54). And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive argument that combines the mutakallimun's doctrine, their proof, and a synthesis with the philosophers' view. It begins by stating the mutakallimun's essential position: events without a beginning are impossible, and all events must trace back to a first event. The author then offers one of their proofs focusing on the nature of motion. The proof runs as follows: The essence (mahiyya) and reality (haqiqa) of motion is that it is a transition from one state to another. Therefore, any motion must be preceded by the state it leaves. In contrast, the essence of pre-eternity (al-azal) and the negation of a beginning require that something not be preceded by anything else. If we suppose a motion existing from pre-eternity, then as a motion it would need to be preceded by something, but as pre-eternal it would need not to be preceded. This is a contradiction, so eternal motion is impossible. Hence, motions must have a first (awwal) and a beginning (bidaya). The author then considers the state before that first motion. Two possibilities exist: either all bodies were non-existent and then came into existence and began moving, or bodies already existed but were stationary and then began moving. In either case, reason demands a cause: in the first case, a creator (mujid); in the second, a mover (muharrik) and director (mudabbir). Thus, in every respect, the motions of the spheres indicate their need for a divine director and mover. The author then notes that both philosophers (who assert eternal motions) and mutakallimun (who assert a first motion) agree on the need for a mover, differing only on the nature of the motions. The passage concludes by showing that on both views—whether motions are eternal or have a beginning—the existence of a God who is neither body nor corporeal is necessary. The verse from the Quran confirms that all creation and command belong to Him.

Key Terms
حوادث لا أول لها
ماهية الحركة
الأزل
الجمع بين النقيضين
أول الحوادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the mutakallimun deny that motion exists altogether.
Correction: They do not deny motion; they deny that motion can be eternal without a beginning. They affirm motion but argue it must have a starting point.

Checkpoint
Why does the mutakallimun argue that motions cannot be eternal?
A) Because motion is an accident that perishes
B) Because the essence of motion requires being preceded by a state, contradicting pre-eternity
C) Because the Quran says so
D) Because philosophers disagree

Key Takeaway
The mutakallimun prove that motion must have a first beginning by showing that eternal motion would combine contradictories.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every motion must have a beginning, including the motions of your body and your will, what does that mean for your own choices? Are they truly your own, or do they trace back to a First Mover? How does this change how you view your actions today?
?
The proof shows that we cannot escape the need for a first beginning of all things. What is the first beginning of your spiritual journey? Have you consciously acknowledged and submitted to that origin? If not, what step can you take today to align your life with the reality that all things began with Allah?
?
Because motion requires a preceding state, your current state is always dependent on what came before. Do you live as though your existence is self-sufficient, or do you constantly remind yourself of your dependence on the Creator? What habit can you practice to let this truth shape your daily attitude?

Allah's Existence
intermediate
6 min
Two Scenarios Before the First Motion and the Necessity of a Divine Mover
The mutakallimun's analysis of the state before the first motion and how both possibilities demand a divine mover, concluding with a synthesis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the mutakallimun, by considering two possible states before the first motion, demonstrate that in either case the universe requires a divine creator, mover, and director.

Core Idea
Whether the universe was created from nothing or existed stationary before moving, both scenarios demand a divine cause.

Having established that motions have a first, the mutakallimun then ask: what was before that first motion? They consider two possibilities: either bodies did not exist and were created, or they existed but were still. In both cases, reason points to a divine being. This lesson explores that reasoning and the synthesis with philosophers.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two possibilities
Before the first motion, either all bodies were non-existent and then created, or they existed but were stationary and then began moving. Read both scenarios.
These exhaust the logical possibilities.
2
See how each leads to God
In the first scenario, creation requires a creator (mujid). In the second, starting motion requires a mover (muharrik) and director (mudabbir).
3
Appreciate the synthesis
Both philosophers (eternal motion) and mutakallimun (finite motion) agree on the need for a divine mover. The passage shows that regardless of whether motion is eternal or has a beginning, God's existence is necessary.
This unifies the two perspectives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن مذهب المتكلمين: أن القول بوجود حوادث لا أول لها محال، وأنه يجب انتهاء الحوادث إلى حادث هو أول الحوادث. ودلائلهم كثيرة سنذكرها في مسألة الحدوث والقدم. إلا أنا نذكر ههنا واحداً من تلك الدلائل، فنقول: إن الدليل على أن الأمر كما ذكرناه: أن ماهية الحركة وحقيقتها: أنها من حالة إلى حالة، وكل ما كان كذلك فإن حقيقته تقتضي أن يكون مسبوقاً بالحالة المنتقل عنها، وكل ما كان كذلك، فإن حقيقته تقتضي تكون مسبوقة بغيرها، فثبت أن حقيقة الحركة وماهيتها تقتضي أن تكون مسبوقة بغيرها. وأما حقيقة الأزل ونفي الأولية فهي تقتضي أن لا تكون مسبوقة بغيرها، وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول: لو فرضنا حركة موجودة في الأزل، فهي لكونها حركة إما أن تكون مسبوقة بغيرها، أو لكونها أزلية يجب أن لا تكون مسبوقة بغيرها. وذلك يوجب الجمع بين النقيضين، وهو محال. فيثبت بهذا البرهان: أنه لا بد للحركات من أول، ومن بداية، وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول: إنه قبل ذلك الوقت الذي هو أول الحركات، إما أن يقال: كانت الأجسام بأسرها معدومة ثم وجدت وتحركت، أو يقال: الأجسام وإن كانت موجودة إلا أنها كانت واقفة ساكنة، فلما جاء ذلك الوقت أحدث في حركاتها وتحركت، فالعقل يقضي بافتقارها إلى الموجد، وأما إن قلنا: إنها كانت موجودة، ولكنها كانت واقفة ثم ابتدأت من ذلك الوقت بالحركة فإن العقل يقضي بافتقارها إلى المحرك والمدير، فثبت أن حركات الأفلاك تدل على افتقارها إلى محرك ومدبر. ويمكن أيضاً أن يقال: هذه الحركات إما أن يقال: إنه لا أول لها، وإما أن يقال: لها أول أيضاً فإن قلنا: إنه لا أول لها وجب افتقارها إلى الإله الذي ليس بجسم ولا بجسماني بالطريق Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if bodies existed stationary before motion, they do not need a creator.
Correction: Even if bodies existed, they needed a mover to initiate motion, as they were incapable of moving themselves.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does reason judge if bodies were existent but stationary before the first motion?
A) They need a creator
B) They need a mover and director
C) They need no cause
D) They are eternal

Key Takeaway
Whether the universe was created from nothing or existed stationary before moving, both scenarios necessitate a divine creator, mover, and director.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your mind might be comfortable with one scenario—either creation from nothing or a pre-existing stationary universe. But the passage forces you to accept that both require God. In what area of your life are you trying to explain things without God, hoping to find a natural cause or coincidence? What would it cost you to admit that God is the ultimate mover behind even your own decisions?
?
The philosophers and mutakallimun agreed on the necessity of a divine being, yet they debated secondary details. Are you more likely to cling to your preferred school of thought rather than accept the common ground they shared? In what way does the unity of the truth demand that you lower your partisan pride and submit to the clear evidence of reason?
